    26	impl View {
    27	    pub fn deduce<V: Vars>(
    28	        matches: &ArgMatches,
    29	        vars: &V,
    30	        strict: bool,
    31	    ) -> Result<Self, OptionsError> {
    32	        let width = TerminalWidth::deduce(matches, vars)?;
    33	        let is_tty = width.actual_terminal_width().is_some();
    34	        let mode = Mode::deduce(matches, vars, is_tty, strict)?;
    35	        let deref_links = matches.get_flag("dereference");
    36	        let follow_links = matches.get_flag("follow-symlinks");
    37	        let total_size = matches.get_flag("total-size");
    38	        let file_style = FileStyle::deduce(matches, vars, is_tty)?;
    39	        Ok(Self {
    40	            mode,
    41	            width,
    42	            file_style,
    43	            deref_links,
    44	            follow_links,
    45	            total_size,
    46	        })
    47	    }
    48	}
    49	
    50	impl Mode {
    51	    /// Determine which viewing mode to use based on the user’s options.
    52	    ///
    53	    /// As with the other options, arguments are scanned right-to-left and the
    54	    /// first flag found is matched, so `exa --oneline --long` will pick a
    55	    /// details view, and `exa --long --oneline` will pick the lines view.
    56	    ///
    57	    /// This is complicated a little by the fact that `--grid` and `--tree`
    58	    /// can also combine with `--long`, so care has to be taken to use the
    59	    pub fn deduce<V: Vars>(
    60	        matches: &ArgMatches,
    61	        vars: &V,
    62	        is_tty: bool,
    63	        strict: bool,
    64	    ) -> Result<Self, OptionsError> {
    65	        let long = matches.get_flag("long");
    66	        let oneline = matches.get_flag("oneline");
    67	        let grid = matches.get_flag("grid");
    68	        let tree = matches.get_flag("tree");
    69	
    70	        if !long && strict {
    71	            Self::strict_check_long_flags(matches)?;
    72	        }
    73	
    74	        if !(long || oneline || grid || tree) {
    75	            if is_tty {
    76	                let grid = grid::Options::deduce(matches);
    77	                return Ok(Self::Grid(grid));
    78	            }
    79	            return Ok(Self::Lines);
    80	        }
    81	
    82	        if long {
    83	            let details = details::Options::deduce_long(matches, vars, strict)?;
    84	
    85	            if grid {
    86	                let row_threshold = RowThreshold::deduce(vars)?;
    87	                let grid_details = grid_details::Options {
    88	                    details,
    89	                    row_threshold,
    90	                };
    91	                return Ok(Self::GridDetails(grid_details));
    92	            }
    93	
    94	            // the --tree case is handled by the DirAction parser later
    95	            return Ok(Self::Details(details));
    96	        }
    97	
    98	        if tree {
    99	            let details = details::Options::deduce_tree(matches, vars);
   100	            return Ok(Self::Details(details));
   101	        }
   102	
   103	        if oneline {
   104	            return Ok(Self::Lines);
   105	        }
   106	
   107	        let grid = grid::Options::deduce(matches);
   108	        Ok(Self::Grid(grid))
   109	    }
   110	
   111	    // TODO: handle that with Clap
   112	    fn strict_check_long_flags(matches: &ArgMatches) -> Result<(), OptionsError> {
   113	        // If --long hasn’t been passed, then check if we need to warn the
   114	        // user about flags that won’t have any effect.
   115	        for flag in &[
   116	            "binary",
   117	            "bytes",
   118	            "inode",
   119	            "links",
   120	            "header",
   121	            "blocksize",
   122	            "time",
   123	            "group",
   124	            "numeric",
   125	            "mounts",
   126	        ] {
   127	            if matches.contains_id(flag) {
   128	                return Err(OptionsError::Useless(flag, false, "long"));
   129	            }
   130	        }
   131	
   132	        if matches.get_flag("git") && !matches.get_flag("no-git") {
   133	            return Err(OptionsError::Useless("git", false, "long"));
   134	        } else if matches.contains_id("level")
   135	            && !matches.get_flag("recurse")
   136	            && !matches.get_flag("tree")
   137	        {
   138	            return Err(OptionsError::Useless2("level", "recurse", "tree"));
   139	        }
   140	
   141	        Ok(())
   142	    }
   143	}

   154	    fn deduce_tree<V: Vars>(matches: &ArgMatches, vars: &V) -> Self {
   155	        details::Options {
   156	            table: None,
   157	            header: false,
   158	            xattr: xattr::ENABLED && matches.get_flag("extended"),
   159	            secattr: xattr::ENABLED && matches.get_flag("security-context"),
   160	            mounts: matches.get_flag("mounts"),
   161	            color_scale: ColorScaleOptions::deduce(matches, vars),
   162	            follow_links: matches.get_flag("follow-symlinks"),
   163	        }
   164	    }
   165	
   166	    fn deduce_long<V: Vars>(
   167	        matches: &ArgMatches,
   168	        vars: &V,
   169	        strict: bool,
   170	    ) -> Result<Self, OptionsError> {
   171	        if strict {
   172	            if matches.get_flag("across") && !matches.get_flag("grid") {
   173	                return Err(OptionsError::Useless("across", true, "long"));
   174	            } else if matches.get_flag("oneline") {
   175	                return Err(OptionsError::Useless("one-line", true, "long"));
   176	            }
   177	        }
   178	
   179	        Ok(details::Options {
   180	            table: Some(TableOptions::deduce(matches, vars)?),
   181	            header: matches.get_flag("header"),
   182	            xattr: xattr::ENABLED && matches.get_flag("extended"),
   183	            secattr: xattr::ENABLED && matches.get_flag("security-context"),
   184	            mounts: matches.get_flag("mounts"),
   185	            color_scale: ColorScaleOptions::deduce(matches, vars),
   186	            follow_links: matches.get_flag("follow-symlinks"),
   187	        })
   188	    }
   189	}

   191	impl TerminalWidth {
   192	    fn deduce<V: Vars>(matches: &ArgMatches, vars: &V) -> Result<Self, OptionsError> {
   193	        if let Some(&width) = matches.get_one("width") {
   194	            if width >= 1 {
   195	                Ok(Set(width))
   196	            } else {
   197	                Ok(Automatic)
   198	            }
   199	        } else if let Some(columns) = vars.get(vars::COLUMNS).and_then(|s| s.into_string().ok()) {
   200	            match columns.parse() {
   201	                Ok(width) => Ok(Set(width)),
   202	                Err(e) => {
   203	                    let source = NumberSource::Env(vars::COLUMNS);
   204	                    Err(OptionsError::FailedParse(columns, source, e))
   205	                }
   206	            }
   207	        } else {
   208	            Ok(Automatic)
   209	        }
   210	    }
   211	}
   212	
   213	impl RowThreshold {
   214	    fn deduce<V: Vars>(vars: &V) -> Result<Self, OptionsError> {
   215	        if let Some(columns) = vars
   216	            .get_with_fallback(vars::EZA_GRID_ROWS, vars::EXA_GRID_ROWS)
   217	            .and_then(|s| s.into_string().ok())
   218	        {
   219	            match columns.parse() {
   220	                Ok(rows) => Ok(Self::MinimumRows(rows)),
   221	                Err(e) => {
   222	                    let source = NumberSource::Env(
   223	                        vars.source(vars::EZA_GRID_ROWS, vars::EXA_GRID_ROWS)
   224	                            .unwrap(),
   225	                    );
   226	                    Err(OptionsError::FailedParse(columns, source, e))
   227	                }
   228	            }
   229	        } else {
   230	            Ok(Self::AlwaysGrid)
   231	        }
   232	    }
   233	}

   235	impl TableOptions {
   236	    fn deduce<V: Vars>(matches: &ArgMatches, vars: &V) -> Result<Self, OptionsError> {
   237	        let time_format = TimeFormat::deduce(matches, vars);
   238	        let flags_format = FlagsFormat::deduce(vars);
   239	        let size_format = SizeFormat::deduce(matches);
   240	        let user_format = UserFormat::deduce(matches);
   241	        let group_format = GroupFormat::deduce(matches);
   242	        let columns = Columns::deduce(matches, vars)?;
   243	        Ok(Self {
   244	            size_format,
   245	            time_format,
   246	            user_format,
   247	            group_format,
   248	            flags_format,
   249	            columns,
   250	        })
   251	    }
   252	}

   254	impl Columns {
   255	    fn deduce<V: Vars>(matches: &ArgMatches, vars: &V) -> Result<Self, OptionsError> {
   256	        let time_types = TimeTypes::deduce(matches)?;
   257	
   258	        let no_git_env = vars
   259	            .get_with_fallback(vars::EXA_OVERRIDE_GIT, vars::EZA_OVERRIDE_GIT)
   260	            .is_some();
   261	
   262	        let git = matches.get_flag("git") && !matches.get_flag("no-git") && !no_git_env;
   263	        let subdir_git_repos =
   264	            matches.get_flag("git-repos") && !matches.get_flag("no-git") && !no_git_env;
   265	        let subdir_git_repos_no_stat = !subdir_git_repos
   266	            && matches.get_flag("git-repos-no-status")
   267	            && !matches.get_flag("no-git")
   268	            && !no_git_env;
   269	
   270	        let file_flags = matches.get_flag("file-flags");
   271	        let blocksize = matches.get_flag("blocksize");
   272	        let group = matches.get_flag("group");
   273	        let inode = matches.get_flag("inode");
   274	        let links = matches.get_flag("links");
   275	        let octal = matches.get_flag("octal-permissions");
   276	        let security_context = xattr::ENABLED && matches.get_flag("security-context");
   277	
   278	        let permissions = !matches.get_flag("no-permissions");
   279	        let filesize = !matches.get_flag("no-filesize");
   280	        let user = !matches.get_flag("no-user");
   281	
   282	        Ok(Self {
   283	            time_types,
   284	            inode,
   285	            links,
   286	            blocksize,
   287	            group,
   288	            git,
   289	            subdir_git_repos,
   290	            subdir_git_repos_no_stat,
   291	            octal,
   292	            security_context,
   293	            file_flags,
   294	            permissions,
   295	            filesize,
   296	            user,
   297	        })
   298	    }
   299	}

   301	impl SizeFormat {
   302	    /// Determine which file size to use in the file size column based on
   303	    /// the user’s options.
   304	    ///
   305	    /// The default mode is to use the decimal prefixes, as they are the
   306	    /// most commonly-understood, and don’t involve trying to parse large
   307	    /// strings of digits in your head. Changing the format to anything else
   308	    /// involves the `--binary` or `--bytes` flags, and these conflict with
   309	    /// each other.
   310	    fn deduce(matches: &ArgMatches) -> Self {
   311	        use SizeFormat::*;
   312	        if matches.get_flag("binary") {
   313	            BinaryBytes
   314	        } else if matches.get_flag("bytes") {
   315	            JustBytes
   316	        } else {
   317	            DecimalBytes
   318	        }
   319	    }
   320	}
   321	
   322	const FORMAT_STYLE_FIELDS: [&str; 6] = [
   323	    "default",
   324	    "iso",
   325	    "long-iso",
   326	    "full-iso",
   327	    "relative",
   328	    "+<CUSTOM_FORMAT>",
   329	];
   330	
   331	impl TimeFormat {
   332	    /// Determine how time should be formatted in timestamp columns.
   333	    pub fn try_from_str(value: &str) -> Result<Self, String> {
   334	        use nu_ansi_term::Color::*;
   335	
   336	        let error_header = format!(
   337	            "invalid value '{}' for '{}'\n  [possible values: {}]\n\n",
   338	            Yellow.paint(value),
   339	            White.paint("--time-style <STYLE>"),
   340	            FORMAT_STYLE_FIELDS
   341	                .map(|s| Green.paint(s).to_string())
   342	                .join(", ")
   343	        );
   344	        let error_footer = format!(
   345	            "\n\nFor more information, try '{}'.\n",
   346	            White.paint("--help"),
   347	        );
   348	
   349	        let fmt = match value {
   350	            "default" => return Ok(TimeFormat::DefaultFormat),
   351	            "iso" => return Ok(TimeFormat::ISOFormat),
   352	            "long-iso" => return Ok(TimeFormat::LongISO),
   353	            "full-iso" => return Ok(TimeFormat::FullISO),
   354	            "relative" => return Ok(TimeFormat::Relative),
   355	            s if !s.starts_with('+') => {
   356	                let error_middle = format!(
   357	                    "{}{}",
   358	                    "Please start the format with a plus sign (+) to indicate a custom format.\n",
   359	                    "For example: \"+%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S\"",
   360	                );
   361	                return Err(format!("{error_header}{error_middle}{error_footer}"));
   362	            }
   363	            s => s,
   364	        };
   365	
   366	        let mut lines = fmt.strip_prefix('+').unwrap().lines();
   367	
   368	        // line 1 is None when there is nothing after `+`
   369	        // line 1 is empty when `+` is followed immediately by `\n`
   370	        let non_recent = match lines.next() {
   371	            None | Some("") => {
   372	                let error_middle = format!(
   373	                    "{}{}",
   374	                    "Custom timestamp format is empty, ",
   375	                    "please supply a chrono format string after the +."
   376	                );
   377	                return Err(format!("{error_header}{error_middle}{error_footer}"));
   378	            }
   379	            Some(non_recent) => non_recent,
   380	        };
   381	
   382	        // line 2 is None when there is not a single `\n`, or nothing after the first `\n`
   383	        // line 2 is empty when there are at least 2 `\n`, and nothing between the 1st and 2nd `\n`
   384	        let recent = match lines.next() {
   385	            Some("") => {
   386	                let error_middle = format!(
   387	                    "{}{}",
   388	                    "Custom timestamp format for recent files is empty, ",
   389	                    "please supply a chrono format string at the second line."
   390	                );
   391	                return Err(format!("{error_header}{error_middle}{error_footer}"));
   392	            }
   393	            recent => recent.map(std::string::ToString::to_string),
   394	        };
   395	
   396	        Ok(TimeFormat::Custom {
   397	            non_recent: String::from(non_recent),
   398	            recent,
   399	        })
   400	    }
   401	}
   402	
   403	impl TimeFormat {
   404	    /// Determine how time should be formatted in timestamp columns.
   405	    fn deduce<V: Vars>(matches: &ArgMatches, vars: &V) -> Self {
   406	        if let Some(arg) = matches.get_one::<TimeFormat>("time-style") {
   407	            arg.clone()
   408	        } else {
   409	            match vars.get(vars::TIME_STYLE) {
   410	                Some(t) if !t.is_empty() => TimeFormat::try_from_str(t.to_str().unwrap_or(""))
   411	                    .unwrap_or(TimeFormat::DefaultFormat),
   412	                _ => Self::DefaultFormat,
   413	            }
   414	        }
   415	    }
   416	}
   417	
   418	impl UserFormat {
   419	    fn deduce(matches: &ArgMatches) -> Self {
   420	        if matches.get_flag("numeric") {
   421	            Self::Numeric
   422	        } else {
   423	            Self::Name
   424	        }
   425	    }
   426	}

   428	impl GroupFormat {
   429	    fn deduce(matches: &ArgMatches) -> Self {
   430	        if matches.get_flag("smart-group") {
   431	            Self::Smart
   432	        } else {
   433	            Self::Regular
   434	        }
   435	    }
   436	}

   443	    /// flag (such as `--modified`) or with a parameter (such as
   444	    /// `--time=modified`). An error is signaled if both ways are used.

   448	    /// see the default set.

   450	        let possible_word = matches.get_one::<TimeArgs>("time");

   453	        let accessed = matches.get_flag("accessed");

    27	        let absolute = *matches.get_one("absolute").unwrap();
    28	
    29	        Ok(Self {
    30	            classify,
    31	            show_icons,
    32	            quote_style,
    33	            embed_hyperlinks,
    34	            absolute,
    35	            is_a_tty,
    36	        })
    37	    }
    38	}
    39	
    40	impl Classify {
    41	    fn deduce(matches: &ArgMatches) -> Self {
    42	        match matches.get_one("classify") {
    43	            Some(ShowWhen::Auto) => Self::AutomaticAddFileIndicators,
    44	            Some(ShowWhen::Always) => Self::AddFileIndicators,
    45	            None | Some(ShowWhen::Never) => Self::JustFilenames,
    46	        }
    47	    }
    48	}
    49	
    50	impl ShowIcons {
    51	    pub fn deduce<V: Vars>(matches: &ArgMatches, vars: &V) -> Result<Self, OptionsError> {
    52	        let force_icons = vars.get(vars::EZA_ICONS_AUTO).is_some();
    53	        let mode_opt = &matches.get_one("icons");
    54	        if !force_icons && mode_opt.is_none() {
    55	            return Ok(Self::Never);
    56	        }
    57	
    58	        match mode_opt {
    59	            Some(ShowWhen::Never) => Ok(Self::Never),
    60	            Some(ShowWhen::Always) => Ok(Self::Always(Self::get_width(vars)?)),
    61	            Some(ShowWhen::Auto) | None => Ok(Self::Automatic(Self::get_width(vars)?)),
    62	        }
    63	    }
    64	
    65	    fn get_width<V: Vars>(vars: &V) -> Result<u32, OptionsError> {
    66	        if let Some(columns) = vars
    67	            .get_with_fallback(vars::EXA_ICON_SPACING, vars::EZA_ICON_SPACING)
    68	            .map(|s| s.to_string_lossy().to_string())
    69	        {
    70	            match columns.parse() {
    71	                Ok(width) => Ok(width),
    72	                Err(e) => {
    73	                    let source = NumberSource::Env(
    74	                        vars.source(vars::EXA_ICON_SPACING, vars::EZA_ICON_SPACING)
    75	                            .unwrap_or("1"),
    76	                    );
    77	                    Err(OptionsError::FailedParse(columns.clone(), source, e))
    78	                }
    79	            }
    80	        } else {
    81	            Ok(1)
    82	        }
    83	    }
    84	}
    85	
    86	impl QuoteStyle {
    87	    pub fn deduce(matches: &ArgMatches) -> Self {
    88	        if matches.get_flag("no-quotes") {
    89	            Self::NoQuotes
    90	        } else {
    91	            Self::QuoteSpaces
    92	        }
    93	    }
    94	}
    95	
    96	impl EmbedHyperlinks {
    97	    fn deduce(matches: &ArgMatches) -> Self {
    98	        if matches.get_flag("hyperlink") {
    99	            Self::On
   100	        } else {
   101	            Self::Off
   102	        }
   103	    }
   104	}

   142	        .arg(arg!(--"git-repos" "list root of git-tree status"))
   143	        .arg(arg!(--"git-repos-no-status" "list each git-repos branch name (much faster)"))
   144	        .arg(arg!(-M --mounts "show mount details (Linux and macOS only)"))
   145	        .arg(arg!(-'@' --extended "list each file's extended attributes and sizes"))
   146	        .arg(arg!(--"no-permissions" "suppress the permissions field"))
   147	        .arg(arg!(--"no-filesize" "suppress the filesize field"))
   148	        .arg(arg!(--"no-user" "suppress the user field"))
   149	        .arg(arg!(--"no-time" "suppress the time field"))
   150	        .arg(arg!(--"no-git" "suppress Git fields (overrides --git, --git-repos, --git-repos-no-status)"))
   151	}
   152	
   153	#[derive(Clone, Debug, PartialEq, Eq)]
   154	pub enum ShowWhen {
   155	    // icons, colors, quotes, headers ? eventually
   156	    Always,
   157	    Auto,
   158	    Never,
   159	}
   160	
   161	impl ValueEnum for ShowWhen {
   162	    fn value_variants<'a>() -> &'a [Self] {
   163	        &[Self::Always, Self::Auto, Self::Never]
   164	    }
   165	
   166	    fn to_possible_value(&self) -> Option<clap::builder::PossibleValue> {
   167	        Some(
   168	            match self {
   169	                Self::Always => "always",
   170	                Self::Auto => "auto",
   171	                Self::Never => "never",
   172	            }
   173	            .into(),
   174	        )
   175	    }
   176	
   177	    fn from_str(s: &str, _ignore_case: bool) -> Result<Self, String> {
   178	        match s.to_lowercase().as_str() {
   179	            "" | "auto" | "automatic" => Ok(Self::Auto),
   180	            "always" => Ok(Self::Always),
   181	            "never" => Ok(Self::Never),
   182	            e => Err(String::from(e)),
   183	        }
   184	    }
   185	}

   200	impl ValueEnum for SortField {
   201	    fn value_variants<'a>() -> &'a [Self] {
   202	        &[
   203	            Self::Name(SortCase::AaBbCc),
   204	            Self::Name(SortCase::ABCabc),
   205	            Self::NameMixHidden(SortCase::AaBbCc),
   206	            Self::NameMixHidden(SortCase::ABCabc),
   207	            Self::Size,
   208	            Self::Extension(SortCase::AaBbCc),
   209	            Self::Extension(SortCase::ABCabc),
   210	            Self::ModifiedDate,
   211	            Self::ModifiedAge,
   212	            Self::ChangedDate,
   213	            Self::AccessedDate,
   214	            Self::CreatedDate,
   215	            #[cfg(unix)]
   216	            Self::FileInode,
   217	            Self::FileType,
   218	            Self::Unsorted,
   219	        ]
   220	    }
   221	
   222	    fn to_possible_value(&self) -> Option<PossibleValue> {
   223	        Some(match self {
   224	            Self::Name(SortCase::AaBbCc) => PossibleValue::new("name").alias("filename"),
   225	            Self::Name(SortCase::ABCabc) => PossibleValue::new("Name").alias("Filename"),
   226	            Self::NameMixHidden(SortCase::AaBbCc) => PossibleValue::new(".name").alias(".filename"),
   227	            Self::NameMixHidden(SortCase::ABCabc) => PossibleValue::new(".Name").alias(".Filename"),
   228	            Self::Size => PossibleValue::new("size"),
   229	            Self::Extension(SortCase::AaBbCc) => PossibleValue::new("ext").alias("extension"),
   230	            Self::Extension(SortCase::ABCabc) => PossibleValue::new("Ext").alias("Extension"),
   231	            // “new” sorts oldest at the top and newest at the bottom; “old” sorts newest at the
   232	            // top and oldest at the bottom. I think this is the right way round to do this:
   233	            // “size” puts the smallest at  the top and the largest at the bottom, doesn’t it?
   234	            Self::ModifiedDate => {
   235	                PossibleValue::new("date").aliases(vec!["time", "mod", "modified", "new", "newest"])
   236	            }
   237	            // Similarly, “age” means that files with the least age (the newest files) get sorted
   238	            //  at the top, and files with the most age (the oldest) at the bottom.
   239	            Self::ModifiedAge => PossibleValue::new("age").aliases(vec!["old", "oldest"]),
   240	            Self::ChangedDate => PossibleValue::new("changed").alias("ch"),
   241	            Self::AccessedDate => PossibleValue::new("accessed").alias("acc"),
   242	            Self::CreatedDate => PossibleValue::new("created").alias("cr"),
   243	            #[cfg(unix)]
   244	            Self::FileInode => PossibleValue::new("inode"),
   245	            Self::FileType => PossibleValue::new("type"),
   246	            Self::Unsorted => PossibleValue::new("none"),
   247	        })
   248	    }
   249	}

   289	        &self,
   290	        cmd: &clap::Command,
   291	        _arg: Option<&clap::Arg>,
   292	        value: &std::ffi::OsStr,
   293	    ) -> Result<Self::Value, Error> {
   294	        match TimeFormat::try_from_str(value.to_str().unwrap()) {
   295	            Err(s) => Err(Error::raw(clap::error::ErrorKind::InvalidValue, s).with_cmd(cmd)),
   296	            Ok(v) => Ok(v),

    45	    /// with the remaining arguments.
    46	    pub fn for_file<'a, 'dir, C>(
    47	        self,
    48	        file: &'a File<'dir>,
    49	        colours: &'a C,
    50	    ) -> FileName<'a, 'dir, C> {

    66	/// When displaying a file name, there needs to be some way to handle broken
    67	/// links, depending on how long the resulting Cell can be.
    68	#[derive(PartialEq, Debug, Copy, Clone)]
    69	enum LinkStyle {
    70	    /// Just display the file names, but colour them differently if they’re
    71	    /// a broken link or can’t be followed.
    72	    JustFilenames,
    73	
    74	    /// Display all files in their usual style, but follow each link with an
    75	    /// arrow pointing to their path, colouring the path differently if it’s
    76	    /// a broken link, and doing nothing if it can’t be followed.
    77	    FullLinkPaths,
    78	}

    80	/// Whether to append file class characters to the file names.

    82	pub enum Classify {
    83	    /// Just display the file names, without any characters.
    84	    #[default]
    85	    JustFilenames,
    86	
    87	    /// Always add a character after the file name depending on what class of
    88	    /// file it is.

    90	
    91	    // Like previous, but only when output is going to a terminal, not otherwise.
    92	    AutomaticAddFileIndicators,

   100	    JustDirectoryNames,

   147	/// A **file name** holds all the information necessary to display the name
   148	/// of the given file. This is used in all of the views.
   149	pub struct FileName<'a, 'dir, C> {
   150	    /// A reference to the file that we’re getting the name of.
   151	    file: &'a File<'dir>,
   152	
   153	    /// The colours used to paint the file name and its surrounding text.
   154	    colours: &'a C,
   155	
   156	    /// The file that this file points to if it’s a link.
   157	    target: Option<FileTarget<'dir>>, // todo: remove?
   158	
   159	    /// How to handle displaying links.
   160	    link_style: LinkStyle,
   161

   165	    mount_style: MountStyle,
   166	}
   167	
   168	impl<C> FileName<'_, '_, C> {
   169	    /// Sets the flag on this file name to display link targets with an
   170	    /// arrow followed by their path.
   171	    #[must_use]
   172	    pub fn with_link_paths(mut self) -> Self {
   173	        if !self.file.deref_links {
   174	            self.link_style = LinkStyle::FullLinkPaths;
   175	        }
   176	        self
   177	    }
   178	
   179	    /// Sets the flag on this file name to display mounted filesystem
   180	    ///details.
   181	    #[must_use]
   182	    pub fn with_mount_details(mut self, enable: bool) -> Self {
   183	        self.mount_style = if enable {
   184	            MountStyle::MountInfo
   185	        } else {
   186	            MountStyle::JustDirectoryNames
   187	        };
   188	        self
   189	    }
   190	}
   191	
   192	impl<C: Colours> FileName<'_, '_, C> {
   193	    /// Paints the name of the file using the colours, resulting in a vector
   194	    /// of coloured cells that can be printed to the terminal.
   195	    ///
   196	    /// This method returns some `TextCellContents`, rather than a `TextCell`,
   197	    /// because for the last cell in a table, it doesn’t need to have its
   198	    /// width calculated.
   199	    #[must_use]
   200	    pub fn paint(&self) -> TextCellContents {
   201	        let mut bits = Vec::new();
   202	        let (icon_override, filename_style_override) = match self.colours.style_override(self.file)
   203	        {
   204	            Some(FileNameStyle { icon, filename }) => (icon, filename),
   205	            None => (None, None),
   206	        };
   207	
   208	        let spaces_count_opt = match self.options.show_icons {
   209	            ShowIcons::Always(spaces_count) => Some(spaces_count),
   210	            ShowIcons::Automatic(spaces_count) if self.options.is_a_tty => Some(spaces_count),
   211	            _ => None,
   212	        };
   213	
   214	        let should_add_classify_char = match self.options.classify {
   215	            Classify::AddFileIndicators => true,
   216	            Classify::AutomaticAddFileIndicators if self.options.is_a_tty => true,
   217	            _ => false,
   218	        };
   219	
   220	        if let Some(spaces_count) = spaces_count_opt {
   221	            let (style, icon) = match icon_override {
   222	                Some(icon_override) => (
   223	                    if let Some(style_override) = icon_override.style {
   224	                        style_override
   225	                    } else {
   226	                        iconify_style(self.style())
   227	                    },
   228	                    icon_override
   229	                        .glyph
   230	                        .unwrap_or_else(|| icon_for_file(self.file))
   231	                        .to_string(),
   232	                ),
   233	                None => (
   234	                    iconify_style(self.style()),
   235	                    icon_for_file(self.file).to_string(),
   236	                ),
   237	            };
   238	
   239	            bits.push(style.paint(icon));
   240	            bits.push(style.paint(" ".repeat(spaces_count as usize)));
   241	        }
   242	
   243	        if self.file.parent_dir.is_none()
   244	            && self.options.absolute == Absolute::Off
   245	            && let Some(parent) = self.file.path.parent()
   246	        {
   247	            self.add_parent_bits(&mut bits, parent);
   248	        }
   249	
   250	        if !self.file.name.is_empty() {
   251	            // The “missing file” colour seems like it should be used here,
   252	            // but it’s not! In a grid view, where there’s no space to display
   253	            // link targets, the filename has to have a different style to
   254	            // indicate this fact. But when showing targets, we can just
   255	            // colour the path instead (see below), and leave the broken
   256	            // link’s filename as the link colour.
   257	            for bit in self.escaped_file_name(filename_style_override) {
   258	                bits.push(bit);
   259	            }
   260	        }
   261	
   262	        if let (LinkStyle::FullLinkPaths, Some(target)) = (self.link_style, self.target.as_ref()) {
   263	            match target {
   264	                FileTarget::Ok(target) => {
   265	                    bits.push(Style::default().paint(" "));
   266	                    bits.push(self.colours.normal_arrow().paint("->"));
   267	                    bits.push(Style::default().paint(" "));
   268	
   269	                    if let Some(parent) = target.path.parent() {
   270	                        self.add_parent_bits(&mut bits, parent);
   271	                    }
   272	
   273	                    if !target.name.is_empty() {
   274	                        let target_options = Options {
   275	                            classify: Classify::JustFilenames,
   276	                            quote_style: QuoteStyle::QuoteSpaces,
   277	                            show_icons: ShowIcons::Never,
   278	                            embed_hyperlinks: EmbedHyperlinks::Off,
   279	                            is_a_tty: self.options.is_a_tty,
   280	                            absolute: Absolute::Off,
   281	                        };
   282	
   283	                        let target_name = FileName {
   284	                            file: target,
   285	                            colours: self.colours,
   286	                            target: None,
   287	                            link_style: LinkStyle::FullLinkPaths,
   288	                            options: target_options,
   289	                            mount_style: MountStyle::JustDirectoryNames,
   290	                        };
   291	
   292	                        for bit in target_name.escaped_file_name(filename_style_override) {
   293	                            bits.push(bit);
   294	                        }
   295	
   296	                        if should_add_classify_char && let Some(class) = self.classify_char(target)
   297	                        {
   298	                            bits.push(Style::default().paint(class));
   299	                        }
   300	                    }
   301	                }
   302	
   303	                FileTarget::Broken(broken_path) => {
   304	                    bits.push(Style::default().paint(" "));
   305	                    bits.push(self.colours.broken_symlink().paint("->"));
   306	                    bits.push(Style::default().paint(" "));
   307	
   308	                    escape(
   309	                        broken_path.display().to_string(),
   310	                        &mut bits,
   311	                        self.colours.broken_filename(),
   312	                        self.colours.broken_control_char(),
   313	                        self.options.quote_style,
   314	                    );
   315	                }
   316	
   317	                FileTarget::Err(_) => {
   318	                    // Do nothing — the error gets displayed on the next line
   319	                }
   320	            }
   321	        } else if should_add_classify_char && let Some(class) = self.classify_char(self.file) {
   322	            bits.push(Style::default().paint(class));
   323	        }
   324	
   325	        if self.mount_style == MountStyle::MountInfo
   326	            && let Some(mount_details) = self.file.mount_point_info()
   327	        {
   328	            // This is a filesystem mounted on the directory, output its details
   329	            bits.push(Style::default().paint(" ["));
   330	            bits.push(Style::default().paint(mount_details.source.clone()));
   331	            bits.push(Style::default().paint(" ("));
   332	            bits.push(Style::default().paint(mount_details.fstype.clone()));
   333	            bits.push(Style::default().paint(")]"));
   334	        }
   335	
   336	        bits.into()
   337	    }
   338	
   339	    /// Adds the bits of the parent path to the given bits vector.
   340	    /// The path gets its characters escaped based on the colours.
   341	    fn add_parent_bits(&self, bits: &mut Vec<ANSIString<'_>>, parent: &Path) {
   342	        let coconut = parent.components().count();
   343	
   344	        if coconut == 1 && parent.has_root() {
   345	            bits.push(
   346	                self.colours
   347	                    .symlink_path()
   348	                    .paint(std::path::MAIN_SEPARATOR.to_string()),
   349	            );
   350	        } else if coconut >= 1 {
   351	            escape(
   352	                parent.to_string_lossy().to_string(),
   353	                bits,
   354	                self.colours.symlink_path(),
   355	                self.colours.control_char(),
   356	                self.options.quote_style,
   357	            );
   358	            bits.push(
   359	                self.colours
   360	                    .symlink_path()
   361	                    .paint(std::path::MAIN_SEPARATOR.to_string()),
   362	            );
   363	        }
   364	    }
   365	
   366	    /// The character to be displayed after a file when classifying is on, if
   367	    /// the file’s type has one associated with it.
   368	    #[cfg(unix)]
   369	    pub(crate) fn classify_char(&self, file: &File<'_>) -> Option<&'static str> {
   370	        if file.is_executable_file() {
   371	            Some("*")
   372	        } else if file.is_directory() {
   373	            Some("/")
   374	        } else if file.is_pipe() {
   375	            Some("|")
   376	        } else if file.is_link() {
   377	            Some("@")
   378	        } else if file.is_socket() {
   379	            Some("=")
   380	        } else {
   381	            None
   382	        }
   383	    }
   384	
   385	    #[cfg(windows)]
   386	    pub(crate) fn classify_char(&self, file: &File<'_>) -> Option<&'static str> {
   387	        if file.is_directory() {
   388	            Some("/")
   389	        } else if file.is_link() {
   390	            Some("@")
   391	        } else {
   392	            None
   393	        }
   394	    }
   395	
   396	    /// Returns at least one ANSI-highlighted string representing this file’s
   397	    /// name using the given set of colours.
   398	    ///
   399	    /// If --hyperlink flag is provided, it will escape the filename accordingly.
   400	    ///
   401	    /// Ordinarily, this will be just one string: the file’s complete name,
   402	    /// coloured according to its file type. If the name contains control
   403	    /// characters such as newlines or escapes, though, we can’t just print them
   404	    /// to the screen directly, because then there’ll be newlines in weird places.
   405	    ///
   406	    /// So in that situation, those characters will be escaped and highlighted in
   407	    /// a different colour.
   408	    fn escaped_file_name<'unused>(
   409	        &self,
   410	        style_override: Option<Style>,
   411	    ) -> Vec<ANSIString<'unused>> {
   412	        let file_style = style_override.unwrap_or(self.style());
   413	        let mut bits = Vec::new();
   414	
   415	        let mut display_hyperlink = false;
   416	        if self.options.embed_hyperlinks == EmbedHyperlinks::On
   417	            && let Some(abs_path) = self
   418	                .file
   419	                .absolute_path()
   420	                .and_then(|p| p.as_os_str().to_str())
   421	        {
   422	            bits.push(ANSIString::from(escape::get_hyperlink_start_tag(abs_path)));
   423	
   424	            display_hyperlink = true;
   425	        }
   426	
   427	        escape(
   428	            self.display_name(),
   429	            &mut bits,
   430	            file_style,
   431	            self.colours.control_char(),
   432	            self.options.quote_style,
   433	        );
   434	
   435	        if display_hyperlink {
   436	            bits.push(ANSIString::from(escape::HYPERLINK_CLOSING));
   437	        }
   438	
   439	        bits
   440	    }
   441	
   442	    /// Returns the string that should be displayed as the file's name.
   443	    fn display_name(&self) -> String {
   444	        match self.options.absolute {
   445	            Absolute::On => std::env::current_dir().ok().and_then(|p| {
   446	                path_clean::clean(p.join(&self.file.path))
   447	                    .to_str()
   448	                    .map(std::borrow::ToOwned::to_owned)
   449	            }),
   450	            Absolute::Follow => self
   451	                .file
   452	                .absolute_path()
   453	                .and_then(|p| p.to_str())
   454	                .map(std::borrow::ToOwned::to_owned),
   455	            Absolute::Off => None,
   456	        }
   457	        .unwrap_or(self.file.name.clone())
   458	    }
   459

    38	
    39	/// Under what circumstances we should display coloured, rather than plain,
    40	/// output to the terminal.
    41	///
    42	/// By default, we want to display the colours when stdout can display them.
    43	/// Turning them on when output is going to, say, a pipe, would make programs
    44	/// such as `grep` or `more` not work properly. So the `Automatic` mode does
    45	/// this check and only displays colours when they can be truly appreciated.
    46	#[derive(PartialEq, Eq, Debug, Copy, Clone)]
    47	pub enum UseColours {
    48	    /// Display them even when output isn’t going to a terminal.
    49	    Always,
    50	
    51	    /// Display them when output is going to a terminal, but not otherwise.
    52	    Automatic,
    53	
    54	    /// Never display them, even when output is going to a terminal.
    55	    Never,
    56	}
    57	
    58	#[derive(PartialEq, Eq, Debug, Default)]
    59	pub struct Definitions {
    60	    pub ls: Option<String>,
    61	    pub exa: Option<String>,
    62	}
    63	
    64	pub struct Theme {
    65	    pub ui: UiStyles,
    66	    pub exts: Box<dyn FileStyle>,
    67	}
    68	
    69	impl Options {
    70	    #[must_use]
    71	    pub fn to_theme(&self, isatty: bool) -> Theme {
    72	        if self.use_colours == UseColours::Never
    73	            || (self.use_colours == UseColours::Automatic && !isatty)
    74	        {
    75	            let ui = UiStyles::plain();
    76	            let exts = Box::new(NoFileStyle);
    77	            return Theme { ui, exts };
    78	        }
    79	
    80	        #[cfg(windows)]
    81	        if nu_ansi_term::enable_ansi_support().is_err() {
    82	            // Failed to enable ansi support, probably because legacy mode console.
    83	            // No need to alert the user unless they explicitly set color=always
    84	            if self.use_colours == UseColours::Always {
    85	                eprintln!("eza: Ignoring option color=always in legacy console.");
    86	            }
    87	            let ui = UiStyles::plain();
    88	            let exts = Box::new(NoFileStyle);
    89	            return Theme { ui, exts };
    90	        }
    91	
    92	        match self.theme_config {
    93	            Some(ref theme) => {
    94	                if let Some(mut ui) = theme.to_theme() {
    95	                    let (exts, use_default_filetypes) = self.definitions.parse_color_vars(&mut ui);
    96	                    let exts: Box<dyn FileStyle> =
    97	                        match (exts.is_non_empty(), use_default_filetypes) {
    98	                            (false, false) => Box::new(NoFileStyle),
    99	                            (false, true) => Box::new(FileTypes),
   100	                            (true, false) => Box::new(exts),
   101	                            (true, true) => Box::new((exts, FileTypes)),
   102	                        };
   103	                    return Theme { ui, exts };
   104	                }
   105	                self.default_theme()
   106	            }
   107	            None => self.default_theme(),
   108	        }
   109	    }
   110	
   111	    fn default_theme(&self) -> Theme {
   112	        let mut ui = UiStyles::default_theme(self.colour_scale);
   113	        let (exts, use_default_filetypes) = self.definitions.parse_color_vars(&mut ui);
   114	        let exts: Box<dyn FileStyle> = match (exts.is_non_empty(), use_default_filetypes) {
   115	            (false, false) => Box::new(NoFileStyle),
   116	            (false, true) => Box::new(FileTypes),
   117	            (true, false) => Box::new(exts),
   118	            (true, true) => Box::new((exts, FileTypes)),
   119	        };
   120	        Theme { ui, exts }
   121	    }
   122	}
   123	
   124	impl Definitions {
   125	    /// Parse the environment variables into `LS_COLORS` pairs, putting file glob
   126	    /// colours into the `ExtensionMappings` that gets returned, and using the
   127	    /// two-character UI codes to modify the mutable `Colours`.
   128	    ///
   129	    /// Also returns if the `EZA_COLORS` variable should reset the existing file
   130	    /// type mappings or not. The `reset` code needs to be the first one.
   131	    fn parse_color_vars(&self, colours: &mut UiStyles) -> (ExtensionMappings, bool) {
   132	        use log::warn;
   133	
   134	        let mut exts = ExtensionMappings::default();
   135	
   136	        if let Some(lsc) = &self.ls {
   137	            LSColors(lsc).each_pair(|pair| {
   138	                if !colours.set_ls(&pair) {
   139	                    match glob::Pattern::new(pair.key) {
   140	                        Ok(pat) => {
   141	                            exts.add(pat, pair.to_style());
   142	                        }
   143	                        Err(e) => {
   144	                            warn!("Couldn't parse glob pattern {:?}: {}", pair.key, e);
   145	                        }
   146	                    }
   147	                }
   148	            });
   149	        }
   150	
   151	        let mut use_default_filetypes = true;
   152	
   153	        if let Some(exa) = &self.exa {
   154	            // Is this hacky? Yes.
   155	            if exa == "reset" || exa.starts_with("reset:") {
   156	                use_default_filetypes = false;
   157	            }
   158	
   159	            LSColors(exa).each_pair(|pair| {
   160	                if !colours.set_ls(&pair) && !colours.set_exa(&pair) {
   161	                    match glob::Pattern::new(pair.key) {
   162	                        Ok(pat) => {
   163	                            exts.add(pat, pair.to_style());
   164	                        }
   165	                        Err(e) => {
   166	                            warn!("Couldn't parse glob pattern {:?}: {}", pair.key, e);
   167	                        }
   168	                    }
   169	                }
   170	            });
   171	        }
   172	
   173	        (exts, use_default_filetypes)
   174	    }
   175	}
   176	
   177	/// Determine the style to paint the text for the filename part of the output.
   178	pub trait FileStyle: Sync {
   179	    /// Return the style to paint the filename text for `file` from the given
   180	    /// `theme`.
   181	    fn get_style(&self, file: &File<'_>, theme: &Theme) -> Option<Style>;
   182	}
   183	
   184	#[derive(PartialEq, Debug)]
   185	struct NoFileStyle;
   186	
   187	impl FileStyle for NoFileStyle {
   188	    fn get_style(&self, _file: &File<'_>, _theme: &Theme) -> Option<Style> {
   189	        None
   190	    }
   191	}
   192	
   193	// When getting the colour of a file from a *pair* of colourisers, try the
   194	// first one then try the second one. This lets the user provide their own
   195	// file type associations, while falling back to the default set if not set
   196	// explicitly.
   197	impl<A, B> FileStyle for (A, B)
   198	where
   199	    A: FileStyle,
   200	    B: FileStyle,
   201	{
   202	    fn get_style(&self, file: &File<'_>, theme: &Theme) -> Option<Style> {
   203	        self.0
   204	            .get_style(file, theme)
   205	            .or_else(|| self.1.get_style(file, theme))
   206	    }
   207	}
   208	
   209	#[derive(PartialEq, Debug, Default)]
   210	struct ExtensionMappings {
   211	    mappings: Vec<GlobPattern>,
   212	}
   213	
   214	#[derive(PartialEq, Debug)]
   215	/// Using a hashmap here for "simple" patterns (plain extensions like '*.txt')
   216	/// improves performance drastically for complex `LS_COLORS` usage (see
   217	/// <https://github.com/eza-community/eza/pull/1421#issuecomment-2816666661>).
   218	///
   219	/// It doesn't change highlighting behavior, as we still walk the
   220	/// [`ExtensionMappings`] in reverse order, and the hashmap will only consist of
   221	/// disjoint sets (it doesn't matter in which order we search *.txt or *.pdf).
   222	///
   223	/// In the event that a pattern shows up twice, we will use the later one (since
   224	/// .insert overrides any entry that exists), which is the correct behavior.
   225	enum GlobPattern {
   226	    Complex(glob::Pattern, Style),
   227	    Simple(HashMap<String, Style>),
   228	}
   229	
   230	impl ExtensionMappings {
   231	    fn is_non_empty(&self) -> bool {
   232	        !self.mappings.is_empty()
   233	    }
   234	
   235	    fn add(&mut self, pattern: glob::Pattern, style: Style) {
   236	        match (self.mappings.last_mut(), is_simple_pattern(pattern)) {
   237	            (Some(GlobPattern::Simple(h)), Ok(s)) => {
   238	                h.insert(s, style);
   239	            }
   240	            (_, Ok(s)) => {
   241	                self.mappings
   242	                    .push(GlobPattern::Simple(HashMap::from([(s, style)])));
   243	            }
   244	            (_, Err(p)) => {
   245	                self.mappings.push(GlobPattern::Complex(p, style));
   246	            }
   247	        }
   248	    }
   249	}
   250	
   251	fn is_simple_pattern(pattern: glob::Pattern) -> Result<String, glob::Pattern> {
   252	    match pattern.as_str().strip_prefix("*.") {
   253	        // Maybe too pessimistic here, some of these might be valid.
   254	        //
   255	        // For example, '*.[*]' is a simple pattern with ext '*'
   256	        // (the [*] is treated as a literal *, not as a glob).
   257	        //
   258	        // Ideally we'd inspect pattern.tokens, but it's not public.
   259	        None => Err(pattern),
   260	        Some(ext) if ext.contains(['?', '*', '[', ']', '.']) => Err(pattern),
   261	        Some(ext) => Ok(ext.to_string()),
   262	    }
   263	}
   264	
   265	// Loop through backwards so that colours specified later in the list override
   266	// colours specified earlier, like we do with options and strict mode
   267	
   268	impl FileStyle for ExtensionMappings {
   269	    fn get_style(&self, file: &File<'_>, _theme: &Theme) -> Option<Style> {
   270	        let maybe_ext = file.name.rsplit_once('.').map(|x| x.1);
   271	
   272	        for mapping in self.mappings.iter().rev() {
   273	            match mapping {
   274	                GlobPattern::Complex(pat, style) => {
   275	                    if pat.matches(&file.name) {
   276	                        return Some(*style);
   277	                    }
   278	                }
   279	                GlobPattern::Simple(map) => {
   280	                    if let Some(ext) = maybe_ext
   281	                        && let Some(style) = map.get(ext)
   282	                    {
   283	                        return Some(*style);
   284	                    }
   285	                }
   286	            }
   287	        }
   288	
   289	        None
   290	    }
   291	}
   292	
   293	#[derive(Debug)]
   294	struct FileTypes;
   295	
   296	impl FileStyle for FileTypes {
   297	    fn get_style(&self, file: &File<'_>, theme: &Theme) -> Option<Style> {
   298	        #[rustfmt::skip]
   299	        return match FileType::get_file_type(file) {
   300	            Some(FileType::Image)      => theme.ui.file_type.unwrap_or_default().image,
   301	            Some(FileType::Video)      => theme.ui.file_type.unwrap_or_default().video,
   302	            Some(FileType::Music)      => theme.ui.file_type.unwrap_or_default().music,
   303	            Some(FileType::Lossless)   => theme.ui.file_type.unwrap_or_default().lossless,
   304	            Some(FileType::Crypto)     => theme.ui.file_type.unwrap_or_default().crypto,
   305	            Some(FileType::Document)   => theme.ui.file_type.unwrap_or_default().document,
   306	            Some(FileType::Compressed) => theme.ui.file_type.unwrap_or_default().compressed,
   307	            Some(FileType::Temp)       => theme.ui.file_type.unwrap_or_default().temp,
   308	            Some(FileType::Compiled)   => theme.ui.file_type.unwrap_or_default().compiled,
   309	            Some(FileType::Build)      => theme.ui.file_type.unwrap_or_default().build,
   310	            Some(FileType::Source)     => theme.ui.file_type.unwrap_or_default().source,
   311	            None                       => None
   312	    };
   313	    }
   314	}

```rust
impl ValueEnum for ShowWhen {
    fn value_variants<'a>() -> &'a [Self] {
        &[Self::Always, Self::Auto, Self::Never]
    }

    fn to_possible_value(&self) -> Option<clap::builder::PossibleValue> {
        Some(
            match self {
                Self::Always => "always",
                Self::Auto => "auto",
                Self::Never => "never",
            }
            .into(),
        )
    }

    fn from_str(s: &str, _ignore_case: bool) -> Result<Self, String> {
        match s.to_lowercase().as_str() {
            "" | "auto" | "automatic" => Ok(Self::Auto),
            "always" => Ok(Self::Always),
            "never" => Ok(Self::Never),
            e => Err(String::from(e)),
        }
    }
}
```

The `from_str` does accept `automatic` but clap may be doing strict checking against `PossibleValue` variants. However, looking at the clap documentation, clap uses `from_str` for parsing. Let me check if there's a `ignore_case` issue:

Actually, looking at this more carefully, clap's `ValueEnum` derive macro typically uses the `to_possible_value` names for validation. The `from_str` is for custom parsing when the `ValueEnum` trait is implemented manually. But clap's `value_parser!(ShowWhen)` should use the `ValueEnum` implementation which includes `from_str`.
